## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (continuous-time population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an explicit time-derivative of population size P, indicating a continuous-time population growth model. Typical structures express growth as P times a per-capita rate that depends on density (P) and/or environmental forcing over time (t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Constant immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (background influx plus proportional growth/decay)
- Power-law per-capita scaling: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (allometric or phenomenological growth with nonlinearity in P)
- Verhulst logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (linear density dependence / carrying capacity behavior)
- Theta-logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible strength/shape of density dependence)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (decelerating per-capita growth roughly proportional to log of density)
- Richards-type generalized logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (extra shape parameter for asymmetric approach to equilibrium)
- Strong crowding (higher-order density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P**3 (multiple competition mechanisms / self-limitation)
- Allee effect (depensation): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth negative at low P, positive at intermediate P, negative at high P)
- Harvesting/removal (effort proportional to abundance): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (exploitation or mortality term added to intrinsic dynamics)
- Saturating harvest (Type II-like removal): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (1 + c3 * P) (catchability saturates at high P)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P * (1 - c4 * P) (periodic environment affecting per-capita growth)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (effective density dependence changes systematically over time)
- Finite-time blow-up (hyperbolic growth): dP_dt = c0 * P**2 (autocatalytic/positive feedback leading to accelerating growth)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP_dt is proportional to P, then the per-capita growth rate (dP_dt / P) is approximately constant ŌåÆ suggests density-independent growth.
- A sign change in dP_dt from positive at low P to negative at high P indicates a stable equilibrium (carrying capacity) ŌåÆ often captured by factors like (1 - c * P) or (1 - (c * P)**theta).
- Per-capita growth rate decreasing approximately linearly with P (i.e., dP_dt/P Ōēł a - b*P) points to logistic-type density dependence.
- If per-capita growth decreases roughly linearly with log(P) (i.e., dP_dt/P Ōēł a - b*log(P)), Gompertz structure dP_dt ŌłØ P*log(K/P) is a natural candidate.
- Negative growth at very low P but positive growth at intermediate P suggests an Allee effect ŌåÆ include a low-density factor like (c*P - 1) multiplying P.
- Multiple curvature changes in dP_dt vs P (e.g., sharper-than-quadratic suppression at high P) suggest higher-order terms (P**3) or theta-logistic exponents.
- Regular oscillations in residuals versus t suggest environmental periodic forcing ŌåÆ add sinusoidal modulation to the per-capita rate (e.g., c0 + c1*sin(c2*t + c3)).
- A long-term drift in growth dynamics over t (e.g., equilibrium level moving) suggests time-varying parameters such as r(t) or K(t) implemented via smooth functions of t (polynomial, exponential, or sinusoidal in t).
- If dP_dt remains negative even at moderate P compared to early times, this can indicate additive mortality/harvesting terms (e.g., -c*P or -c*P/(1+c*P)) layered on top of intrinsic growth.
